  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c5540a6e-9d6a-4764-b550-6e1a7eca3c04'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_96268933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96268933" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1542839-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228753802p2/1542839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96268933?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/1542839-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780756400309" href="/book/show/481866.Sea_of_Silver_Light">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">shut-ins, prisoners</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1542839-mike?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96268933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17337560768425111237">This book, the fourth in a four-book fantasy series, is an amazing example of how a good idea can be stretched and diluted until it is no longer pleasurable to read. There is nothing particularly wrong with the Otherland series. The ideas are interesting, the execution is fairly creative, some of the characters are competently developed, etc. But it is clear that the objective of the author (and the editor/publisher) was to create a large series (measured by the heft of the books and the number </span>
  <span id="freeText17337560768425111237" style="display:none">This book, the fourth in a four-book fantasy series, is an amazing example of how a good idea can be stretched and diluted until it is no longer pleasurable to read. There is nothing particularly wrong with the Otherland series. The ideas are interesting, the execution is fairly creative, some of the characters are competently developed, etc. But it is clear that the objective of the author (and the editor/publisher) was to create a large series (measured by the heft of the books and the number of trees killed), rather than to tell a good story. <br /><br />This could have been a fantastic effort if edited to about a 1000 pages or so. But the padding and circumlocution required to turn it into four 1000-page books makes reading it annoying. Instead of more things happening, you have the same number of plot events stretched slowly out. <br /><br />The style of the chapters, in which we return again and again for brief glimpses of the action, only makes the sense of non-action worse. <br /><br />I will say this - if you were on some kind of long vacation, or holed up in a room for a while, or whatever, and you wanted something to read, this series would kill a lot of time. Otherwise, you have things to do with your life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17337560768425111237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1402194970" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1402194970" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1402194970?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/25944350-sea-of-silver-light">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1402194970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15250334882014779380"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This series is a monster, and thankfully after all those hours, it comes to an enjoyable conclusion.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> Yup, George Newbern is still excellent. I might have liked this series less in text due to the slow parts, but Mr. Newbern really brings the world and it's characters to life in a way that put him up there in the top tier of audiobook narrators for me.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>This review will be a bit lighter than it probably would have been had I written it a month ago. Time </span>
  <span id="freeText15250334882014779380" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This series is a monster, and thankfully after all those hours, it comes to an enjoyable conclusion.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> Yup, George Newbern is still excellent. I might have liked this series less in text due to the slow parts, but Mr. Newbern really brings the world and it's characters to life in a way that put him up there in the top tier of audiobook narrators for me.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />This review will be a bit lighter than it probably would have been had I written it a month ago. Time sort of got away from me this month and I've fallen badly behind on my reviews.<br /><br />Much like other books in this series, I found the plot a bit slow in places, but by the last third things were moving along at such a pace that I hate to stop. Thankfully I got to listen to the last 6 or so hours in one sitting.<br /><br />The world building is once again the star for me. However several of the characters have become quite dear to me after so many hours spent with them, especially !Xabbu and Fredricks. Renie still annoyed me at times, but far less than in previous books. So obviously she's grown on me too.<br /><br />I am sad I'll no longer be wandering through the vast expanse of Otherland with our little troupe of explorers, but I'm happy for the time I got to spend with them.<br /><br />If you're a fan of cyberpunk and epic fantasy, this series to me was just about the perfect blend of those things. I felt that things were wrapped up nicely leaving you wanting more, but satisfied that there isn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15250334882014779380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15451656207218461253" style="display:none">No matter how many times I read this (or this, fifth time, listen to it on audiobook) I still fall so hard for this book, and this series, that it's an emotional pain when I get to the end. <span id="freeTextContainer7242693035738950877">This is one of the worst books I have ever read.<br/><br/>Its particularly bad because the series started with such amazing promise; the first book is literally brilliant. The next two were pretty mediocre; well-written, but ultimately travelogue-fantasy without any plot. Characters just stumbled from interesting locale to interesting locale and ended up right back where they started from. But this last book is terrible. I was literally shouting out loud in the street when I read the climax, it was that b</span>
  <span id="freeText7242693035738950877" style="display:none">This is one of the worst books I have ever read.<br /><br />Its particularly bad because the series started with such amazing promise; the first book is literally brilliant. The next two were pretty mediocre; well-written, but ultimately travelogue-fantasy without any plot. Characters just stumbled from interesting locale to interesting locale and ended up right back where they started from. But this last book is terrible. I was literally shouting out loud in the street when I read the climax, it was that bad. Deus Ex Machina meets the "skillful" plot-twistings of Independence Day bad. I wrote Tad Williams a letter just to tell him it was that bad - something I have never done to another author in my long life full of books. Less than 60 pages from the end of the multiple-thousand-page series, he introduces a new character (hinted at before of course, but never met) who ends up responsible for almost everything that has happened so far. A character whose grand plan is the electronic equivalent of avoiding door-to-door salesmen by throwing yourself in a blender - needlessly, since a skin sample would do - processing the resulting sludge to decode your DNA, writing your DNA sequence down on paper using ancient aramaic in invisible ink, putting that paper in a bottle, and throwing it in the ocean with the hope that someday someone will find it and reconstruct you. Except its less likely to work. Exponentially so.<br /><br />Its so bad that years later, when I went to go write a review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28694.Shadowmarch__Shadowmarch___1_" title="Shadowmarch (Shadowmarch, #1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadowmarch</a> (which is really quite good,) just thinking about it made me angry enough to come back and write this.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1214471582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1214471582" />
    <a title="terpkristin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3392444-terpkristin"><img alt="terpkristin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438465987p2/3392444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1214471582?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="terpkristin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="terpkristin" href="/user/show/3392444-terpkristin">terpkristin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=sffaudio">sffaudio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3392444-terpkristin?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1214471582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1385760471716055725">Audiobook from Penguin Audio<br/>Narrated by George Newbern<br/>Length: 37.75 hours<br/><br/>The finale to the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/43762-otherland' rel='nofollow noopener'>Otherland</a> series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10092.Sea_of_Silver_Light__Otherland___4_' title='Sea of Silver Light (Otherland, #4) by Tad Williams' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sea of Silver Light</a> wraps up the multitude of story lines that began in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28695.City_of_Golden_Shadow__Otherland___1_' title='City of Golden Shadow (Otherland, #1) by Tad Williams' rel='nofollow noopener'>City of Golden Shadow</a>. While the book dragged in places, and some may find that the book (and the series, especially in the middle books) wanders a bit too much, it is hard not to appreciate Tad Williams' amazingly prescient series, especially if you're a fan of a) the internet and b) classic literature. It's probably</span>
  <span id="freeText1385760471716055725" style="display:none">Audiobook from Penguin Audio<br />Narrated by George Newbern<br />Length: 37.75 hours<br /><br />The finale to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43762-otherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Otherland</a> series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10092.Sea_of_Silver_Light__Otherland___4_" title="Sea of Silver Light (Otherland, #4) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">Sea of Silver Light</a> wraps up the multitude of story lines that began in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28695.City_of_Golden_Shadow__Otherland___1_" title="City of Golden Shadow (Otherland, #1) by Tad Williams" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Golden Shadow</a>. While the book dragged in places, and some may find that the book (and the series, especially in the middle books) wanders a bit too much, it is hard not to appreciate Tad Williams' amazingly prescient series, especially if you're a fan of a) the internet and b) classic literature. It's probably safe to say that the wandering will not be for everybody, but for those that enjoy the mystery and the references to other works, the series could be a lot of fun.<br /><br />A series written in the mid-late 90's, the books cover amazing breadth of topics with a wide cast of characters in this world and in a parallel online world. What started as a cyberpunk story quickly unfolded into a much larger world with many players with significantly different motivations--on all sides of the story. With unlikely/atypical heroes (a South African woman, an African "bushman", a blind woman, two teenagers, a mom, and a guy who doesn't know his own past, not to mention a 5 or 6-year old girl, an ancient man...the cast is huge!) and a sprawling world, it's easy to see why some people are overwhelmed. The more intriguing part, though, is trying to piece together the entire story, trying to figure out who's involved in the world and for what purpose...and what the online world really is. I will admit that when the world was pieced together, it seemed pretty out there...but I was so engrossed that I didn't really mind. The only part I really <i>did</i> mind was the end; the book felt maybe a little too neat, and a little too drawn out at the end. That said, it does leave an opening for Williams to return to the world (and looking on Goodreads, it seems as if he may have done just that with a short story in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77563.Legends_II" title="Legends II by Robert Silverberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Legends II</a>.<br /><br />It's hard to describe the book and what happened in the series without venturing into spoiler territory. Basically, Renie, a young South African woman who is a sort of professor or teacher of computer engineering-type classes at a local university, finds one day that her brother is in a coma of sorts, a result of playing an online game. Games in the future world that Williams created are played online in a virtual reality simulation type schema, where users have different levels of gear that immerse them (fully or to varying degrees) into a virtual world. Some users go so far as to get neural cannulas, so that they can "jack in" and have the VR system provide a direct link to their brain, become fully immersed. Renie, wanting to try to find out more about how her brother came to be in the coma, went online to try to learn what she could of what he got into. Unsurprisingly, she found herself sucked into and literally stuck in a virtual world, unable to disconnect (sort of like Sword Art Online). While there, she meets others who have family members with the same affliction as her brother, and still others who have been recruited by an unknown agent to help Renie and those who are trying to help their children/family members. In parallel, there is the story of the Grail Brotherhood, a private group of the world's most powerful and wealthiest elite, who wish to achieve immortality, and invest heavily in a system to do so. In a third story line, there is additional intrigue about a psychopath who calls himself "Dread" and seems to seek out ways to torture and kill others, online and in reality. His story ends up weaving and in some ways connecting the Grail Brotherhood and those of the people trying to help the children. Throughout, there are a multitude of worlds created by various users of the online system, many with literary references (such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/236093.The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz__Oz___1_" title="The Wonderful Wizard of Oz (Oz, #1) by L. Frank Baum" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds" title="The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Worlds</a>) or other evolving schema (such as a virtual rainforest that actually begins to evolve in the simulation world, similar to how it might have on earth). Williams uses cyberpunk, the idea of virtual/simulation worlds, and some more fantastical elements (some characters have special abilities, particularly abnormal/special mental powers) to weave a tale that leaves the reader picking up puzzle pieces and slowly piecing things together, just as the heroes do in the story.<br /><br />I'm most amazed at how prescient Williams was. The book was written in the mid-90's, yet there are references to things in the world today, innovations that were barest ideas of science fiction in the 90's. The first and most obvious observation is that the VR world, while more immersive than anything we really have today, is very much akin to the internet of today, with people spending entire lives and making entire livelihoods on the internet. People use tablet-like devices to connect to the networks, to make calls, to shop, to go into their simulation worlds--much like an iPad or other tablet of today. People watch movies on the internet, so-called "Net Flicks" (I really wonder if that's how Netflix's name came to be), and an automated robotic floor-sweeping robot (Roomba, anyone) makes an appearance or two. Kids have "storybook sunglasses" which sound a bit like more immersive (and frankly more fun) versions of Google Glass. Just today, I read <a href="http://science.slashdot.org/story/15/05/29/2028238/hacking-your-body-through-a-nerve-in-your-neck" rel="nofollow noopener">an article on Slashdot about body hacking through the vagal nerve</a><a></a>, a topic that's actually brought up in the book (as a therapy that is abused, oddly enough). There are other examples, which reading in 2015, are fun nuggets to pick up along the way. It's crazy how forward-thinking this book was, how much it got "right" even for 2015 (I think the book is supposed to take place closer to 2050).<br /><br />I liked this book and really enjoyed the series. I think that listening was a fantastic way to experience the book, to be able to lay back and shut my eyes and become immersed in the book as the characters are immersed in their world. The narration was (as I've said in my other reviews) great, if a little slow. But that meant that I could speed the book up slightly in the playback, cutting down some of the listening time.<br /><br />The book (and series) may not be for everyone. I think it's fair to criticize this book for going on a little "too long" or for being a little "too neat," and it's equally fair to think that Book 1 started slow or that books 2 and 3 wandered a bit (they absolutely were "middle books" in a series, which not everybody enjoys). But I still really liked the series. I look forward to reading it again in the future, maybe in a few years, to see how much I can pick up in advance, knowing as I do now, how the book ends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1385760471716055725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer676383859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12999124983153830427">An exciting conclusion, I loved it.<br/><br/>Everything falls apart at the close of Mountain of Black Glass (Otherland #3), and now the unlikely heroes of the Otherland system are scattered far and wide in the heart of the dying operating system and beyond. Renie, !Xabbu, and Fredericks are stuck with unlikely allies in the evil Felix Jongleur and the brain damaged Ricardo Klement. But even this tenuous partnership is shattered when the virtual world shatters, and Renie finds herself stranded in an amorph</span>
  <span id="freeText12999124983153830427" style="display:none">An exciting conclusion, I loved it.<br /><br />Everything falls apart at the close of Mountain of Black Glass (Otherland #3), and now the unlikely heroes of the Otherland system are scattered far and wide in the heart of the dying operating system and beyond. Renie, !Xabbu, and Fredericks are stuck with unlikely allies in the evil Felix Jongleur and the brain damaged Ricardo Klement. But even this tenuous partnership is shattered when the virtual world shatters, and Renie finds herself stranded in an amorphous landscape with the doddering Klement her only companion. <br /><br />Martine, Paul Jonas, T4b, and Florimel find themselves back in the already terrifying bug world, made even worse with horrifically human-bug mutations on the loose, mutations whose sole desire is to rip them limb from limb. Not even the benevolent Kunohara seems to be able to hold off the writhing masses for long. <br /><br />In the real world, things are becoming truly scary for little Christabel. Her daddy learns of Mr. Sellers and now the entire family, plus Sellers, the boy Cho Cho and the lawyer Catur Ramsey, end up on the run together. But they can't run forever... <br /><br />Meanwhile Dulcie Anwin awakens from her fledgling crush on Johnny Dread into growing unease and fear, even as he begins to show her the romantic attention she has long desired. Dread himself revels in both the virtual destruction of the Otherland realms and the terrorization of the Other itself, the effects of which are felt keenly by those still trapped within the system. <br /><br />Finally, Long Joseph, Jeremiah, and Del Rey find themselves under siege, the military stronghold under the mountain no longer the sanctuary they'd thought it to be. It's only a matter of time before Dread's mercenaries break through the base's defenses, and all the three have to defend themselves are a single gun with three bullets and none among them skilled enough to make them count.<br /><br />This is perhaps the most edgy installment of the Otherland series. Everything seems to be falling apart and danger stalks the heroes and the villains at every turn. No one is safe, and still the children lie comatose in their hospital beds. Will the destruction of the Otherland network spell their doom?<br /><br />I love this book and the series that spawned it. You'll find no plot holes in this series, everything, even those things that seemed insignificant in the other books, finds a purpose in Otherland #4. I highly recommend this book to anyone who loves sci fi and has the time and patience to tackle such a massive work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12999124983153830427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText6094102985682270830" style="display:none">10/10<br /><br />With Sea of Silver Light the magic journey in the Otherland series comes to an end and with Tad Williams having made a wonderful finale in, perhaps, one of his best book to date but also one of my most favorite.<br /><br />In this book Williams manages to close the series very beautiful as through his complex world-building and his, truly, countless characters has made a really strong story with lots of twist and revelations that will change radically the course of the protagonists, and also many, wonderful, moments of action and suspense.<br />Williams’ writing on the other hand, even though the astonishing size of the book and the series in general, flows really well and also manages to make you love, not only all the characters but his incredible ideas too.<br /><br />Highly recommended!!!<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1262227639?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher" href="/user/show/7077333-christopher">Christopher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101524336" href="/book/show/10754890-sea-of-silver-light">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1262227639&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1262227639" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11283965720083601681">Sea of Silver Light is the next book in the series and has our characters finally getting to grips with their opposition and overcoming them! :D This was hinted at and heavily set up in the previous book with the gang encountering the 'Other' directly for the first as well being scattered to a mountain top! :D Understandably this gives and sets a number of big challenges for this book and sets you wondering as to what the characters are going to be put through as the book progresses as the size </span>
  <span id="freeText11283965720083601681" style="display:none">Sea of Silver Light is the next book in the series and has our characters finally getting to grips with their opposition and overcoming them! :D This was hinted at and heavily set up in the previous book with the gang encountering the 'Other' directly for the first as well being scattered to a mountain top! :D Understandably this gives and sets a number of big challenges for this book and sets you wondering as to what the characters are going to be put through as the book progresses as the size of the book hints at big things which certainly keep popping up! :D <br /><br />It is very hard throughout to actually guess what is going to happen to the main characters but the broad gist of the plotline can be guessed but how and what characters will make it through the book are always questions that you find yourself asking throughout! :D Sea of Silver Light is totally unpredictable throughout but the way that the characters and their relationships end up is really great for most of them and Sea of Silver Light has some clever twists at the end both before they manage to leave the network and after which also gets to show us how the characters are up to in the world after their adventures and also adds a lot of light moments such as when they check their bank accounts and find who has survived not to mention the odd sentient life form discovered! :D<br /><br />Sea of Silver Light makes for a awesome part in the series with you really routing for the characters and also wanting to see the comeuppance for certain characters which eventually does come with some great plot twists! :D<br /><br />The whole scale of the Otherland reality though forms a great backdrop for many of the plot twists that take place with many of the events set up in the previous books coming to fruition and you will realise as you read how far back some of these things have been set up but there are most certainly plenty of 'Ahha' moments that will have you puzzling over where things will go as well as the books often as they do coming back to the subject of space exploration! :D One of the humorous things throughout the book though is how the 'good' team without realizing it co-opt the Grail Brotherhoods immortality machine essentially without realizing it which lends itself to a lot of humour and also the way certain worlds and other books are liberally used will have you laughing as well which to the characters and the reader comes as a very big relief as at some points the characters are never allowed a moment's break battling various sym worlds so this helps to give some of the characters their just rewards! :D<br />The addition throughout of chapter beginnings that show the state of general society at the time also puts things into context for many of the characters and you can see society heading that way if companies had their way! :o<br /><br />Overall will keep you up page turning as you will really want to find out what happens! :D <br /><br />Brilliant stuff and highly recommended! :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="11283965720083601681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_169420887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169420887" />
    <a title="Aleah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3398219-aleah"><img alt="Aleah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436270185p2/3398219.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169420887?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aleah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aleah" href="/user/show/3398219-aleah">Aleah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3398219-aleah?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169420887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12757936562492850827">In "Sea of Silver Light," book four in the "Otherland" tetrology, Tad Williams wraps up his massive sci-fi saga. <br/><br/><strong>Four big books in eight medium-sized sentences:</strong><br/>In a not so distant future children across the globe are being lost to unexplainable comas. For South African college professor Renie Sulaweyo, whose baby brother Stephen is among those affected, the horror of this epidemic is all too real. Researching Stephen's condition leads Renie to the Otherland, a massively complex virtual reality n</span>
  <span id="freeText12757936562492850827" style="display:none">In "Sea of Silver Light," book four in the "Otherland" tetrology, Tad Williams wraps up his massive sci-fi saga. <br /><br /><strong>Four big books in eight medium-sized sentences:</strong><br />In a not so distant future children across the globe are being lost to unexplainable comas. For South African college professor Renie Sulaweyo, whose baby brother Stephen is among those affected, the horror of this epidemic is all too real. Researching Stephen's condition leads Renie to the Otherland, a massively complex virtual reality network that is powered by a nearly sentient operating system known as the Other. Its architects? A secretive group of affluent and aged elites who refer to themselves as the Grail Brotherhood. In an attempt to save Stephen, Renie and her friend, !Xabbu, find a way into this exclusive network. Once in Otherland the pair discover others on similar quests... and one whose ambitions are the stuff of nightmares. Our adventurers soon learn that they are trapped in the Otherland and, although the environments are simulated, the dangers are all too real. <br /><br /><strong>My take:</strong><br />I had a great time following the characters as they progressed through their adventures in this series. They were an interesting and diverse collection of protagonists and their various relationships (both romantic and not) tugged at my heartstrings. My favorite character was Orlando, a teenager suffering from the late stages of Progeria. Orlando uses the virtual reality environment of the Net to experience a freedom that he was denied in his dying body. I don't want to give too much away, but I feel that Orlando was the true hero of this series.<br /><br />The virtual world where most of this story takes place allowed Williams to stretch the boundaries of science fiction. Purely fantastical worlds existed in an entirely science fiction based virtual reality environment, making for a fun mix of the genres. The best of both worlds in my humble opinion. The plot is delightfully intricate and the page count just goes on and on. Loved it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12757936562492850827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_389651219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/389651219" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2935621-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318005507p2/2935621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/389651219?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/2935621-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer389651219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16151244749868721616">The four books of this series took me most of the last 6 months as I honestly found them somewhat of a slog at the beginning. I'm not really sure I would have stuck with it had the series not come highly recommended, but I'm extremely glad I fought my initial instinct. I became increasingly attached to the characters as they encountered the frustration, hope and challenges of an impossible quest in an environment beyond their control. Initially I thought the quest within the virtual world would </span>
  <span id="freeText16151244749868721616" style="display:none">The four books of this series took me most of the last 6 months as I honestly found them somewhat of a slog at the beginning. I'm not really sure I would have stuck with it had the series not come highly recommended, but I'm extremely glad I fought my initial instinct. I became increasingly attached to the characters as they encountered the frustration, hope and challenges of an impossible quest in an environment beyond their control. Initially I thought the quest within the virtual world would have been predictable, mundane and full of old fashioned guesswork of future technology advances. What surprised me was not only the accuracy the world parallels the current direction of technology issues facing our society, but also the ability to reign in the technology to match the reality of a not too distant future. For instance there are no flying cars, teleportation, space travel, replicators and so on.<br /><br />This final book in the series pulled everything together and as one would expect in a 1000 page novel, no stone was left unturned. I always enjoy a good epilogue after the main quest ends and there was certainly lots of explanation to fill in any gaps from the story readers might have had throughout the series. If I have any criticism it would probably be that this series could have been cut down by about 30% in length, however that extra bit of detail arguably gives you intimate insights into the characters and their backgrounds which are usually only touched on in most novels. Ironically, it is quite possible this extra detail was ultimately what ended up pulling me into the series.<br /><br />I'm quite sure it will be a while before I read another Tad Williams book, but I definitely feel richer for having read and experienced this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16151244749868721616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5197761664312571349">Otherland is the first fantasy series that I've finished this year (I've read a few other book #1s with no intention of continuing, including Tad William's own slogfest MS&T). I started a topic that got pretty long many years back about fantasy series that ended somewhere between well and spectacular. It didn't turn out to be a very long list. Otherland isn't going on it. It wasn't terrible, it just wore out its welcome. The least interesting character ended up being the hinge point of the entir</span>
  <span id="freeText5197761664312571349" style="display:none">Otherland is the first fantasy series that I've finished this year (I've read a few other book #1s with no intention of continuing, including Tad William's own slogfest MS&amp;T). I started a topic that got pretty long many years back about fantasy series that ended somewhere between well and spectacular. It didn't turn out to be a very long list. Otherland isn't going on it. It wasn't terrible, it just wore out its welcome. The least interesting character ended up being the hinge point of the entire plot (which really went off the rails). The main character of the first book that pulled me into the story ended up not actually having much to do, plot-wise. As happens with long series, I kept reading out of curiosity for what happens with book 1 characters while not caring about characters introduced later and finding time spent with a few of the later characters to be an annoying distraction.<br /><br />If you want to read Otherland, I recommend stopping when the settings and characters start losing their magic.The start of the story depended heavily on a "sense of wonder" advanced technology is indistinguishable from magic, with success, but became repetitive and brought in too many convenient or out of nowhere powers and coincidences too many times by the end. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5197761664312571349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16347983748037012182">Compelling characters and a plotline that could be the envy of any writer. Best books I've read in a good while.   <span id="freeText16347983748037012182" style="display:none">Compelling characters and a plotline that could be the envy of any writer. Best books I've read in a good while. The teenage netslang was a bit off sometimes, but that's not why I gave the last book of the Otherland series 4 stars - it's the ending. Everybody gets their reward, all the baddies are duly punished :yawn: a bit like Sunday school. It sort of killed the whole story for me. <br /><br />SPOILER<br /><br />Did the author absolutely have to resurrect Orlando? He was one of my favorite characters and when Sam dreams about talking with Orlando and then thinks that it's just her talking to herself afterall, is one of the saddest moments that I've lived through in literature and I've had my share of books. It breaks your heart without being melodramatic or cheesy. Now all of this moment's drama and depth is taken away and cheapened by a resurrected hologram Orlando at the end, dwelling eternally in his private LOTR heaven and I ask again; was this absolutely necessary? I feel disappointed and a bit cheated. I wouldn't have minded reading a version with the end chopped off. </span>

<div id="review_257011225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257011225" />
    <a title="Ricky Ganci" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5628971-ricky-ganci"><img alt="Ricky Ganci" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589290938p2/5628971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257011225?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricky Ganci" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricky Ganci" href="/user/show/5628971-ricky-ganci">Ricky Ganci</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780756400309" href="/book/show/481866.Sea_of_Silver_Light">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257011225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12319734652006109047">And with the final volume, Williams loses me. 300 pages of overwritten, tripish, hyper-explained and muddled plot through bizarre fantasy worlds that just seem to be there for the author’s enjoyment really pissed me off, and I’m throwing in the towel, feeling like I’ve wasted the last month of my life reading a story that I’ve not come to care about in any gorram way. I will not read anything else that he has written, and I cannot see how so many people find this volume of the series to be so un</span>
  <span id="freeText12319734652006109047" style="display:none">And with the final volume, Williams loses me. 300 pages of overwritten, tripish, hyper-explained and muddled plot through bizarre fantasy worlds that just seem to be there for the author’s enjoyment really pissed me off, and I’m throwing in the towel, feeling like I’ve wasted the last month of my life reading a story that I’ve not come to care about in any gorram way. I will not read anything else that he has written, and I cannot see how so many people find this volume of the series to be so uncritically good. This book was a joke—his writing style beat out of me every ounce and every iotus of care that I had for any of the characters, and since I can’t find a concise summary of the ending on the Internet, I’m just going to not care at all. I feel let down, pissed off, and REALLY glad that I only bought two of the books at full price. These books did NOT need to be this long. Tad Williams, you’re my least favorite fantasy author. Otherland sucks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12319734652006109047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2678454995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2678454995" />
    <a title="Steve R" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51602729-steve-r"><img alt="Steve R" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550608435p2/51602729.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2678454995?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve R" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve R" href="/user/show/51602729-steve-r">Steve R</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2678454995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3587418759279106260">At last I've finished rereading this magnum opus. (Somehow, Goodreads deleted my January 2005 approximate date of original reading, and I've no idea how to put it back). This final volume, at just over a thousand pages, required even more of an arduous effort than any of its predecessors in the series, and though there were certain high points along the way, the overall impression I had was an overwhelmingly tepid one.<br/><br/>Williams REALLY made an effort with this book and with the series in general t</span>
  <span id="freeText3587418759279106260" style="display:none">At last I've finished rereading this magnum opus. (Somehow, Goodreads deleted my January 2005 approximate date of original reading, and I've no idea how to put it back). This final volume, at just over a thousand pages, required even more of an arduous effort than any of its predecessors in the series, and though there were certain high points along the way, the overall impression I had was an overwhelmingly tepid one.<br /><br />Williams REALLY made an effort with this book and with the series in general to pull off a vast amalgam of several different thematic analyses. However, to a large degree, the work impressed me as just a frustratingly difficult story of the struggles of the small, weak and relatively powerless against the exceptionally strong forces of selfishness, greed, lust for power and pure evil. Sure, the culmination of the struggles gave some solace by the end of the book, but for page after page after page, I was overwhelmed by one dominant emotion: sadness.<br /><br />The dwarves in Mother Goose land come back after being away for a day to find their town, their homes and their wives all gone, as the Ending inexorably progresses. When Dulcie tries to help an East European woman who is being physically abused in the street, she is told by the woman to leave her be, and after she chases her abuser away, sees the victim run after him. ChoCho has a feeling that his life with the 'mamapapa' group of Christabel's family will not end well for him, and decides he'll have to run away. Martine is overwhelmed by remorse when she hears of the probable fate of the Wicked Tribe from Bonnie Mae Simpkins, and after the culminating triumphs at the end of the book, finds it difficult to share in the celebratory mood since, as she claims 'the pain was so great'. Renie, remembering !Xabbu's song 'This place is now a sad place for me/Because the string is broken' puts a lyrical spin to this semi-constant impression of loss and powerlessness which, despite the narrative's ending, is the dominant impression I came away with from the novel.<br /><br />Certainly, Williams knows how to keep his juggling balls of plot lines dancing to the reader's delight. At one point well into the work Dread takes on both Dulcie and Calliope while almost at the same time, in the network, his sim is advancing menacingly on Martine and her friends, the odious Mudd is climbing out of his vat in order to menace the unsuspecting Olga while those tied through the Other to the satellite in space are threatened by Jongleur's plan to initiate the Apep Sequence with being blasted into deep space. Suspense is one element over which Williams has assured mastery.<br /><br />But it is his overall theme that he has let get away from him, much to the novel's detriment. You can tell he certainly believes in the essential righteousness of the Bushmen's symbiotic relationship with nature, and its startling contrast to the screaming lunacy of much of our modern electronic world. His introductory news flashes of often sordid moral, scarily violent, cravenly selfish business practices and self-serving political movements bespeak a jaded view of the modern world and its developing problems. But I found this very poorly reflected in the actual plot of the novel, which often boiled down to a David and Goliath type of struggle between the miniscule forces of good and the overarching powers of evil.<br /><br />And it was in the heart of this uneven struggle that I found a weakness of his story telling. Firstly, he commits the unpardonable sin of all potboiler type writers in not revealing all to his reader soon enough, so that what the actual truth while known to the characters is kept hidden from the reader. At a critical point, Sellars reveals to Ramsay what he's discovered about the mysterious Other (the operating system of the Grail network), an explanation which leaves Ramsay reeling but the reader mystified. Later, Sellars makes a similarly major revelation to Olga about the being we will come to know as Daniel, but once again, Olga's astonishment is all the reader has to go on at the point. Why be so obviously obtuse and recalcitrant about your revelations?<br /><br />Finally, the outcomes of both Dread and Jongleur, the two arch villains of this over one thousand page work (or three thousand if you count the whole series), were each dealt with in such a brief, cursory, vague and/or fleetingly indirect manner as to leave me wondering both what had actually happened and why it seemed to lack such a dramatic punch as such thoroughly despicable characters certainly deserved. Also, the essential background information of the character who was the first to be introduced in volume one is not given until about three quarters of the way through this fourth volume. A little more respect for his reader's right to know would have certainly increased my respect for Williams as a writer.<br /><br />All in all, an amazing effort, but still one which could have been much better. A tighter narrative arc (i.e., about two thousand less pages!), a ramping up of his social-political themes and greater respect for his reader's rights would all have improved upon this nonetheless outstanding effort.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3587418759279106260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14147231" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/858949-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14147231?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/858949-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780886779771" href="/book/show/165508.Sea_of_Silver_Light">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=top-shelf">top-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14147231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14214993317583767766">At last we have come to the end of our journey, when all will be explained and all will be resolved.<br/><br/>As the book opens, the Other - the operating system for the Grail Brotherhood's mysterious plan for immortality - has been defeated, overcome and overpowered by the truly evil assassin Dread. With his mutant ability to manipulate electronics, Dread has taught the Other how to feel true pain, and now has nearly complete control over the Otherland network. With a nearly limitless number of worlds to</span>
  <span id="freeText14214993317583767766" style="display:none">At last we have come to the end of our journey, when all will be explained and all will be resolved.<br /><br />As the book opens, the Other - the operating system for the Grail Brotherhood's mysterious plan for immortality - has been defeated, overcome and overpowered by the truly evil assassin Dread. With his mutant ability to manipulate electronics, Dread has taught the Other how to feel true pain, and now has nearly complete control over the Otherland network. With a nearly limitless number of worlds to choose from, Dread allows his sadistic madness to run wild. But no matter how many worlds he rapes and plunders, there are still those he truly wants to destroy - the Otherland explorers sent by the mysterious half-human Sellars.<br /><br />But those explorers themselves face greater dangers than Dread. Half of them have been thrust back into the twisted realms of Otherland, where the horrors and dangers that had been built into it have mutated into unrecognizable terrors. The other half... they ended up in the heart of the Other's secret dreams. There they must face the eventual death of the network and survive it, if they can.<br /><br />Offline, Sellars has brought all of his players into position. Lawyers, children and old women are his army, and together they will uncover the horrible and heartbreaking truth about the nature of the Other and the evil that has been done to it.<br /><br />I really love this series. As it moves towards its ending, which does involve a lot more explaining than most other books do, it's easy to get swept up in the sheer scale of the narrative. There's a lot to take in by the end of the series, a lot of loose ends to tie up, but it all wraps up rather nicely. More or less. There is a rather major revelation that comes near the end that just kind of... gets written off. I have a sneaking suspicion that Williams might have been able to stretch this series into a fifth book, but it probably would have suffered from Rowling Syndrome - a lot of unnecessary padding in between the important bits.<br /><br />The important thing is that, by the end of the book you really do feel invested in the world that Williams has created. You care about the characters, and you want everything to turn out all right for them. For the good ones, at least. For the bad ones, you want them to get their just desserts, to see them suffer as they have made others suffer. You even find yourself feeling for the Other, which we - and the protagonists - have always believed to be the main villain of the story. It is not, as we find out, and the scope of the villainy that has been done to it is truly astonishing.<br /><br />In his forward to the second book, Williams apologized to his readers about the cliffhanger ending to the first. This isn't really four books, he said - it's one giant book that had to, for various reason, be split into four. The main reason, of course, being that no one would print or buy a 3,500 page hardcover, even if the fine folks at DAW Books were willing to try it. He is right, though - it is one very long story, and thus you can extract a great many things from it, if you want to.<br /><br />There's no one thing that I can say this book is about. In one sense, it is an exploration of the future of the digital world and what it might mean to people. The virtual net of this story would be as alien to us as the internet would be to our grandparents. It has become the sea in which our characters swim, and their main way of interacting with the world. It is only when their ability to go offline is taken away from them that they truly begin to value the world and the identity they've left behind. What's more, it explores how we connect with each other - looking at both the relationships we build in virtual space and the ones we build in the real world, and finding complete validity in them both.<br /><br />There are issues of identity, best shown by Orlando, whose towering Thargor the Barbarian character hides a young teenager with a crippling illness that will kill him long before he's old enough to vote. His best friend has a slightly less unfortunate secret to share - that behind those big, muscular sim bodies, Sam Fredericks is actually a girl.<br /><br />The story explores issues of family - how Renie deals with her father, Long Joseph Sulaweyo, or how little Christabel Sorenson's family react when they find out that their young daughter has been drawn deep into Sellars' conspiracy. And the bonds between mother and child that can never truly be broken.<br /><br />And there are even issues of the very definition of the word "life." If your mind is perfectly copied into a computer, with all its memories and personality intact, is it still you? Are you still human? Are you even alive, in any real sense? The Grail Brotherhood certainly believed so, or they would never have started this project in the first place. But in a system as broad and complicated as the Otherland network, who knows what else might arise to test our definition?<br /><br />The story is about heroism and history, about love and hate, about the unshakable bonds of friendship and the tenuous reliance on people you despise. It's about the lengths to which fear will drive you and the extremes you will encounter when you test that fear. It's about science and faith and looking at the world in ways you never imagined. It's about good, it's about evil.<br /><br />It's about life, really, and what it is about life that makes us want more of it.<br /><br />Now I'm just waxing philosophical. To sum up: this is probably one of my favorite stories in my library. I highly recommend you pick it up, set some time aside, and enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14214993317583767766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1597129871" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1597129871" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1597129871?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781841490649" href="/book/show/10091.Sea_of_Silver_Light">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597129871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18148328597459309678">So, this book is the final one in the Otherland series and I am so happy that I have not only finished the series, but also been enthralled the whole way through and excited for the ending. In this final Volume you really start to see all the threads Tad Williams has so far set up coming brilliantly together and all the characters reaching different places...<br/><br/>This story as a whole is set in a world where Virtual reality is not longer and aspiration but rather a part of life. Everyone has a hook-u</span>
  <span id="freeText18148328597459309678" style="display:none">So, this book is the final one in the Otherland series and I am so happy that I have not only finished the series, but also been enthralled the whole way through and excited for the ending. In this final Volume you really start to see all the threads Tad Williams has so far set up coming brilliantly together and all the characters reaching different places...<br /><br />This story as a whole is set in a world where Virtual reality is not longer and aspiration but rather a part of life. Everyone has a hook-up to the Net and even the poorer people have some limited access. The world has been irrevocably changed and people can live much of their lives connected to machines and living in VR. It's a wonderful concept and marvellous idea, but when some people start to go into comas whilst connected to the Net, their loved ones and relatives decide they need to find out why and they stumble across Otherland. Otherland is a Network unlike all the others, everything seems real as life, and everything is connected. The team of character within Otherland need to try and uncover its secrets, whilst everyone on the outside is waiting to see just what they find... <br /><br />The whole way through reading this series it has been a story which grew on me page by page. Whilst I felt at first that the characters and concept were strong, book 1 ended so suddenly I just HAD to go straight onto book 2. I then found out that Tad Williams considers this series to be a series where every book is connected to make one overall story, rather than being sequential like most book series.<br /><br />The story in this book is full of new worlds, new challenges, new fights and dilemmas. I really found that I was gripped by the story and unable to get it out of my head in the in-between time when I wasn't able to read it.<br /><br />In particular, I thinks Sea of Silver Light really confronts some of the relationships - both healthy and unhealthy - which we have so far seen, and I loved that. I also felt as though this one was the book which made me most emotional whilst reading it (whilst I was on the train and couldn't just start bawling). There are some truly wonderful sentiments raised in this series and also some heartwarming and devastating moments. <br /><br />The characters are the heart and soul of why these books work so well for me becuase each of them felt so unique and genuine and real. You can tell that Williams has done his homework in finding out about each of these people's cultures and implementing that into his story. <br />Renie &amp; !Xabbu are favourites of mine becuase Renie is a fighter and she never, ever gives up that fight even when things continue to take turns for the worse. !Xabbu is a truly mystical and interesting character for me. He has a sense of tribal culture and heritage surrounding him as he's originally from the Bushamen Tribes, and I loved his stories in the book.<br />Orlando and Fredricks are also a pair of friends who I found fun to read about and easy to enjoy. Both of them come from very different real-life situations but they have formed a very strong bond of friendship by playing games together on the Net. I loved the memories they shared and also seeing them both have to deal with some horrible situations as they're both wonderfully bad-ass when they need to be.<br />Christabel &amp; Sellers are an entirely different duo, one being a very young child and one and elderly man. Their 'friendship' is definitely the one which took me the longest time to uncover, yet the whole time that I was deciphering it I was absorbed in the story and found it entirely fascinating!<br />Martine is a character who stands alone as someone to admire becuase of her raw strength of character and the evident challenges she's had in life. I honestly loved her diary entries in this book and the previous becuase it just added another layer to her character complexity and I think she's great.<br />Paul Jonas is such a sad character for the majority of this series becuase he has lost his memories and cannot fathom how he has been 'put' into a realm of simulations and mad-worlds. Jonas is a character who I constantly felt strong empathy for as you really didn't know exactly what his story was, becuase he didn't, and uncovering it became fairly vital as the story went on. <br />There are many others I could also mention but this is most of the important ones and the ones which I found myself most attached to and excited by.<br /><br />On the whole although these books are long I loved each and every one and moment. I felt like these books truly captivated me and my attention whilst reading, and this is the first Sci-fi series where I've actually got to the end, let alone marathon-ed my way through! All of the these books combine to become and excellent story and for me, I wouldn't change it. I loved the pacing, loved the worlds and imagination of Williams, and I just felt it was awesome. A 5* read for sure! I would highly recommend checking this one out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18148328597459309678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_704138913" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/704138913" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17410641-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360707349p2/17410641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/704138913?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/17410641-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17410641-david?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17410641-david?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704138913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11339704975592340719">God, this was big, she [Renie] thought... Page 896, Vol IV of Otherland.<br/><br/>Renie, I couldn't agree more! It was big in many ways: ambition, scope of imagination, depth of characterization and like !Xabbu's stories, there are 'big' points to ponder.<br/><br/>The story is complex and satisfying. Each thread is tied up nicely and without being too trite, each getting what they deserve. <br/><br/>Some might find the enormous quantity of text to plow through daunting, but it gave each facet of this story enough room to dev</span>
  <span id="freeText11339704975592340719" style="display:none">God, this was big, she [Renie] thought... Page 896, Vol IV of Otherland.<br /><br />Renie, I couldn't agree more! It was big in many ways: ambition, scope of imagination, depth of characterization and like !Xabbu's stories, there are 'big' points to ponder.<br /><br />The story is complex and satisfying. Each thread is tied up nicely and without being too trite, each getting what they deserve. <br /><br />Some might find the enormous quantity of text to plow through daunting, but it gave each facet of this story enough room to develop properly and fit into a logical whole. <br /><br />This volume, the fourth, with it's position as conclusion doesn't suffer as much from a fault that the other volumes (particularly II &amp; III) have of a seeming endless cycle of the heroes being found by the villains, being chased, narrowly avoiding capture, being found by the villains... and all the while learning slightly more information, but without context. Even though each simworld Mr. Williams described was fantastic and each chase had it's own brilliant aspect of creativity, nevertheless the overall pattern became a predictable exercise. Although you could not guess what exactly would be chasing them, how and though what fantastic location, you had the distinct impression of being there before. <br /><br />Hats off to the development of each of the heroes! Each one changed in a gradual, believable manner. That is to say not too much. No one was born again... Well, only literally. ;)<br /><br />Last point: Mr. Williams through the story and the faux newsfeed at the start of each chapter raises many ethical questions that are on the agenda of our 21st century. The most important for this work being: What is real life? If code passes the Turing Test and exists in all five of our senses and fits almost all the criteria we have for life, is it life?<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I do think that data beings at the end with Sellars entire mea culpa are, although interesting in light of the ethical issues brought up in the book, not needed. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />A good series, this volume being the best. If you are a marathon reader, that is all 26 miles and 385 yards of it, through the uphills and the down, then get started! You have an exciting journey ahead: many strange lands to visit and people to meet. <br /><br />Thank you, Mr. Williams! I have enjoyed your work and will continue reading your amazing stories.</span>

<div id="review_154143677" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154143677" />
    <a title="Peter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5121917-peter"><img alt="Peter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300056489p2/5121917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154143677?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/5121917-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781841490649" href="/book/show/10091.Sea_of_Silver_Light">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154143677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13995133949568658584">A wonderful, climactic conclusion of a great story: It's essential you read the first three books because the story is continuous. Tad Williams amazes you by his ability to bring together all the ingredients of the previous three books and then tie them up very neatly indeed! There have been largely eight different narratives going on in the previous three books and they all come together without the process being contrived or predictable. Added to that, there is real pace in the story. I couldn</span>
  <span id="freeText13995133949568658584" style="display:none">A wonderful, climactic conclusion of a great story: It's essential you read the first three books because the story is continuous. Tad Williams amazes you by his ability to bring together all the ingredients of the previous three books and then tie them up very neatly indeed! There have been largely eight different narratives going on in the previous three books and they all come together without the process being contrived or predictable. Added to that, there is real pace in the story. I couldn't put this book down towards the end. Chapters leave you with exciting cliffhangers and twists to the story that you will never guess. I also found several parts of the ending really very moving. His characters are so realistic and interesting that you totally care about these people. I think one of the things I like about his story is that his characters are unconventional yet people you can relate too. He has created a real super villain in the form of John Dread, but not in a stereotyped way. He is utterly evil and we are able to see through that particular glass very darkly indeed in this story. What other reviewers might comment upon slows down the story I feel actually makes the book. Williams' attention to detail is remarkable. Landscapes come and go but you are never left with anything other than a perfect picture of where the story takes place. Otherworld is a Virtual Reality universe made special by its processing power to create absolute belief in the environment the visitor is in. Tad William's descriptive powers have exactly the same effect! This is a brilliant story and I strongly recommend it to you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13995133949568658584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
