<div id="review_117735664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117735664" />
    <a title="johanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/877298-johanna"><img alt="johanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1202233921p2/877298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117735664?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="johanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="johanna" href="/user/show/877298-johanna">johanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117735664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12902612178723722843">i could not put these books down. as he says in the forward to the second book- this is actually one very long book written into four books. i LOVED this book. i read the first one completely by chance and as soon as i finished it i had to immediately order the other three. these books have taken over my life for the last few months. any spare moment i had the book was in my hand. i dreamed about the books, i thought about the characters, i felt a part of the adventure. i haven't been this satis</span>
  <span id="freeText12902612178723722843" style="display:none">i could not put these books down. as he says in the forward to the second book- this is actually one very long book written into four books. i LOVED this book. i read the first one completely by chance and as soon as i finished it i had to immediately order the other three. these books have taken over my life for the last few months. any spare moment i had the book was in my hand. i dreamed about the books, i thought about the characters, i felt a part of the adventure. i haven't been this satisfied in a very long time. Tad Williams is truly an incredible writer. there was so much detail, so many characters and plot lines to follow but he did a beautiful job weaving everything together. and for a person that never likes to leave questions opened i was so satisfied that every little twist and plot and question was answered even with more surprises on the way. it is such a complex story with so many interwoven stories and i loved that about it. it was as complex as life itself and really brought to light how our own lives our stories that we weave together. the near future aspect of the story is also wonderful and haunting. i think we are not so far from the technologies and politics and conspiracies that surround this series. these books were thought provoking and totally engrossed me. it's a perfect melding of sci-fi and fantasy. i just can't say enough about this series. i am totally overtaken and will be thinking of these characters and the stories for a long time to come. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12902612178723722843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94757120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94757120" />
    <a title="Andres" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2207574-andres"><img alt="Andres" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291712952p2/2207574.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94757120?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andres" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andres" href="/user/show/2207574-andres">Andres</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207574-andres?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94757120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7958128627753216435">Finally the end! All is revealed!<br/><br/>Really though, everything is explained in this final volume (as you would hope). And while on the surface it is a satisfying conclusion, it may just be the natural high in reaction to finishing the darn thing. Some 3300 pages and it's done!<br/><br/>As I mentioned in reviews about the first three parts, verbiage is plentiful and there are plenty of maddening delays in answer giving. Then, when the answers come, they are heavy in info dumping exposition. Aren't we ever happ</span>
  <span id="freeText7958128627753216435" style="display:none">Finally the end! All is revealed!<br /><br />Really though, everything is explained in this final volume (as you would hope). And while on the surface it is a satisfying conclusion, it may just be the natural high in reaction to finishing the darn thing. Some 3300 pages and it's done!<br /><br />As I mentioned in reviews about the first three parts, verbiage is plentiful and there are plenty of maddening delays in answer giving. Then, when the answers come, they are heavy in info dumping exposition. Aren't we ever happy readers? Yes and no.<br /><br />My biggest problem was that at the very end there are these new... I wouldn't call them characters, but there are these things that seem to be important to one of the characters, and everyone as a group is suddenly called on to make a life or death decision about these heretofore unknown things, and while it seems to be a weighty and difficult decision, for the me as a reader I couldn't really have given a damn. We are introduced to these things at (practically) the last minute---why would we care about what they decide? The characters we've read about in the preceding 3200 pages have our attention and sympathy (maybe), so why care about these things after only a couple of pages?<br /><br />Final verdict: Awesome, epic, world-building, cyber something adventure. But also detailed, long, and at times slow. <br /><br />I was thinking of reading the Wheel of Time series... but I seriously doubt I will now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7958128627753216435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_909720470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/909720470" />
    <a title="Adobe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/406207-adobe"><img alt="Adobe" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/909720470?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adobe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adobe" href="/user/show/406207-adobe">Adobe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer909720470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer678657935399099251">I really loved the first book of the <i>Otherland</i> quartet, <i>City of Golden Shadow</i>, which was deliriously crammed with cool ideas about the near future and old culture. Which is why <i>Sea of Silver Light</i> leaves such a bitter taste in my mouth: on its own, it would just be a grey slog with painstakingly explains its every charm into the ground, but as the culmination of a once promising series, it's an insult. There is no lacking for closure in this book; closure lurks around every corner, but the offer</span>
  <span id="freeText678657935399099251" style="display:none">I really loved the first book of the <i>Otherland</i> quartet, <i>City of Golden Shadow</i>, which was deliriously crammed with cool ideas about the near future and old culture. Which is why <i>Sea of Silver Light</i> leaves such a bitter taste in my mouth: on its own, it would just be a grey slog with painstakingly explains its every charm into the ground, but as the culmination of a once promising series, it's an insult. There is no lacking for closure in this book; closure lurks around every corner, but the offered explanations and conclusions aren't satisfying. I was willing to go with William's submerged thesis of the first book -- stories exist independently from mankind -- but by the time he's spelling it all out in mile-high letters in <i>Sea of Silver Light</i>, I was ready to bail.</span>
  <a data-text-id="678657935399099251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('COdcQIy6d5zPzpg+oV8JjLdVEt/K8K7YobuXiawMLv2bwcByywmhmrF4YPXTlBSzEQUEItOnxNf/x2FgP1jOBw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4WRnUMl8Z3E10sgHzVz69Jlj4N0ibfUhM+dtMBB5IRFyQvtijs+xd0tkMMy/l+fLPzP2IDs6ny5tm5vZgy3B6w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

From the moment the Bush team took office and decided to retain Clarke in his post as the counterterrorism czar, Clarke tried to persuade them to take al Qaeda as seriously as had Bill Clinton. For months, he was denied the opportunity even to make his case to Bush. He encountered key officials who gave the impression that they had never heard of al Qaeda; who focused incessantly on Iraq; who even advocated long-discredited conspiracy theories about Saddam\'s involvement in previous attacks on the United States.  Clarke was the nation\'s crisis manager on 9/11, running the Situation Room -- a scene described here for the first time -- and then watched in dismay at what followed. After ignoring existing plans to attack al Qaeda when he first took office, George Bush made disastrous decisions when he finally did pay attention. <span id="freeTextContainer6971866796399103562">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an</span>
  <span id="freeText6971866796399103562" style="display:none">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an MMO on steam.com. Tad is currently immersed in the creation of ‘The Last King of Osten Ard’, planned as a trilogy with two intermediary novels. He, his family and his animals live in the Santa Cruz mountains in a suitably strange and beautiful house. @tadwilliams @mrstad</span>

Do we not take the raw stuff of chaos and impose a beginning, middle, and end on it, like the simplest and most profound of folktales, to reflect the shapes of our own tiny lives? And if the physicists are right, that the physical world changes as it is observed, and we are its only known observers, then might we not be bending the entire chaotic universe, the eternal, ever-active Now, to fit that familiar form?&rdquo;</span>
